<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">New World Order (professional wrestling)</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>New World Order</b> (commonly abbreviated <b>NWO</b>, in logo stylized as <b>nWo</b>) was a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestling</a> <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#S" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">stable</a> that originally consisted of <a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan" title="Hulk Hogan">"Hollywood" Hulk Hogan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Nash" title="Kevin Nash">Kevin Nash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Hall" title="Scott Hall">Scott Hall</a>, best known for their appearances in <a href="/wiki/World_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Championship Wrestling">World Championship Wrestling</a> (WCW) from the mid to late 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_original_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_original-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The stable originated in WCW with the <a href="/wiki/Gimmick_(professional_wrestling)" title="Gimmick (professional wrestling)">gimmick</a> of a group of unsanctioned wrestlers aiming to "<a href="/wiki/Takeover#Hostile_takeovers" title="Takeover">take over</a>" and control WCW in the manner of a <a href="/wiki/Gang" title="Gang">street gang</a>. The group later appeared in the <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">World Wrestling Federation</a> (WWF) after the purchase of WCW by the WWF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup> A similar group, known as The Band, appeared in <a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling" title="Total Nonstop Action Wrestling">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling</a> (TNA) in 2010; although a resurrection of the nWo was implied, this group was never billed as such in TNA, since WWE owns the rights to this trademark.</p>
<p>The nWo <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Angle" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">angle</a> became one of the most influential forces in the mid-to-late 1990s success of WCW and was instrumental in turning mainstream North American professional wrestling back into a more mature, adult-oriented product and became the main driving forces behind WCW topping WWF in the <a href="/wiki/Monday_Night_Wars" title="Monday Night Wars">Monday Night Wars</a>. Based on the <a href="/wiki/UWF_International" title="UWF International">Union of Wrestling Forces International</a> (UWFi) invasion angle in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Japan_Pro_Wrestling" title="New Japan Pro Wrestling">New Japan Pro Wrestling</a> (NJPW) and fueled initially by the unexpected <a href="/wiki/Heel_(professional_wrestling)" title="Heel (professional wrestling)">villainous</a> <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Turn" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">turn</a> of Hulk Hogan, the nWo storyline is generally considered one of the most successful angles in the history of modern-day professional wrestling, spawning several imitations and parodies, including groups such as the <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_World_Order" title="The Blue World Order">bWo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_World_Order" title="Latino World Order">lWo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juggalo_World_Order" title="Juggalo World Order">jWo</a>. The group dominated WCW programming throughout the late-1990s and continued its domination until the dissolution of WCW in 2001, during which time there were several, sometimes rival incarnations of the group.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concept">Concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The nWo storyline was an idea created by WCW Executive Vice President <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bischoff" title="Eric Bischoff">Eric Bischoff</a>, whose inspiration for the angle came after attending <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Japan_Pro_Wrestling" title="New Japan Pro Wrestling">New Japan Pro Wrestling</a>'s Battle Formation show at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Dome" title="Tokyo Dome">Tokyo Dome</a> on April 29, 1996. The show was headlined by a NJPW vs. UWFi match for the <a href="/wiki/IWGP_Heavyweight_Championship" title="IWGP Heavyweight Championship">IWGP Heavyweight Championship</a>, as New Japan's <a href="/wiki/Shinya_Hashimoto" title="Shinya Hashimoto">Shinya Hashimoto</a> defeated UWFi's <a href="/wiki/Nobuhiko_Takada" title="Nobuhiko Takada">Nobuhiko Takada</a>. Bischoff wanted to do an invasion-type angle where WCW was being sabotaged by another wrestling group, initially insinuated as being the WWF, since the nWo's founding members had previously wrestled for the company. The nWo was originally portrayed as a separate entity from WCW. Often, <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a>-style vignettes and product commercials concerning the nWo were presented in the style of a <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_signal_intrusion" title="Broadcast signal intrusion">broadcast signal intrusion</a>, with a voice proclaiming, "The following announcement has been paid for by the New World Order".</p>
<p>Others, such as <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Nash" title="Kevin Nash">Kevin Nash</a>, television <a href="/wiki/Television_director" title="Television director">director</a> <a href="/wiki/Craig_Leathers" title="Craig Leathers">Craig Leathers</a>, chief WCW <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Book" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">booker</a> <a href="/wiki/Terry_Taylor" title="Terry Taylor">Terry Taylor</a>, and Taylor's assistants <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Sullivan_(wrestler)" title="Kevin Sullivan (wrestler)">Kevin Sullivan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Orndorff" title="Paul Orndorff">Paul Orndorff</a>, all contributed their own ideas to the nWo concept.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Championship_Wrestling_.281996-2000.29">World Championship Wrestling (1996-2000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: World Championship Wrestling (1996-2000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation">Formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Outsiders_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Outsiders (professional wrestling)">The Outsiders</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nwo-outsiders.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="487" data-file-width="649" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Nwo-outsiders.jpg/220px-Nwo-outsiders.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Nwo-outsiders.jpg/330px-Nwo-outsiders.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Nwo-outsiders.jpg/440px-Nwo-outsiders.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nwo-outsiders.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Scott_Hall" title="Scott Hall">Scott Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Nash" title="Kevin Nash">Kevin Nash</a> posed as invaders looking to take over <a href="/wiki/World_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Championship Wrestling">WCW</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On May 19, 1996, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Nash" title="Kevin Nash">Kevin Nash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Hall" title="Scott Hall">Scott Hall</a> wrestled their final matches for the WWF as Diesel and Razor Ramon, respectively, as they both had opted to sign with rival WCW instead of staying with the promotion. Eight days after his last WWF appearance, Hall appeared in <a href="/wiki/Macon,_Georgia" title="Macon, Georgia">Macon, Georgia</a> for the May 27 <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Monday_Nitro" title="WCW Monday Nitro">Nitro</a></i> which was emanating from the <a href="/wiki/Macon_Coliseum" title="Macon Coliseum">Macon Coliseum</a>. As <a href="/wiki/Mike_Enos" title="Mike Enos">The Mauler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Doll" title="Steve Doll">Steve Doll</a> wrestled, Hall emerged from the crowd and entered the ring, bringing the match to a halt, and called for the ring announcer's microphone. "You all know who I am", Hall said to the stunned crowd, "but you don't know why I'm here". He went on to deliver the "You Want a War?" speech, stating that he and unnamed allies had a challenge for WCW Executive Vice President <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bischoff" title="Eric Bischoff">Eric Bischoff</a> and any WCW wrestlers. As the episode neared its end, Hall accosted Bischoff, who was also the lead broadcaster for Nitro at the time, in the broadcast booth and demanded that he tell WCW owner <a href="/wiki/Ted_Turner" title="Ted Turner">Ted Turner</a> to pick three of his best wrestlers for "a war".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw96_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-wcw96-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwopage_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwopage-6">[6]</a></sup> The next week, Hall claimed to have a "big surprise" for fellow professional wrestler <a href="/wiki/Sting_(wrestler)" title="Sting (wrestler)">Sting</a>. On the following <i>Nitro</i>, the big surprise was revealed to be <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Nash" title="Kevin Nash">Kevin Nash</a>. They were dubbed <a href="/wiki/The_Outsiders_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Outsiders (professional wrestling)">The Outsiders</a>, randomly appearing at WCW events to cause trouble and inevitably be led out of the building by WCW security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw96_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-wcw96-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-outsiders_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-outsiders-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1692" data-file-width="799" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg/140px-Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg/210px-Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg/280px-Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Razor_Ramon_posing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hall as Razor Ramon, whose antics led <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWF</a> to fear that WCW had <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property_infringement" title="Intellectual property infringement">infringed on their intellectual property</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite the fact that Hall and Nash were both fully employed by WCW, the storyline's implication that they were WWF wrestlers "invading" WCW was enough of a concern to the WWF that it considered legal action over Hall and Nash's antics. Hall was the bigger concern to the WWF, as he had not fully distanced himself from his Razor Ramon character, continuing to act like Razor and speaking with Razor's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_American" title="Cuban American">Cuban American</a> accent. WCW attempted to address these concerns at <a href="/wiki/The_Great_American_Bash#1996" title="The Great American Bash">The Great American Bash</a> in June 1996. Bischoff promised them a match at the next <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-view" title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a> event, and then directly asked both Hall and Nash if they were employed by the WWF, to which they both said no.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The WWF, still unsatisfied, filed a lawsuit, claiming that Bischoff had proposed inter-promotional matches that would air on <a href="/wiki/TBS_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="TBS (U.S. TV channel)">TBS</a>, associating the two <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Promotion" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">promotions</a> with each other. Also at The Great American Bash, both Hall and Nash pressed Bischoff to name his company's three representatives for their impending match. Bischoff said that he had found three men who would answer their challenge, but would not name them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw96_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-wcw96-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100megs_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-100megs-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Bischoff held a draft on Nitro to determine WCW's representatives, and Sting, <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luger" title="Lex Luger">Lex Luger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">Randy Savage</a> were chosen.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hostile_takeover">Hostile takeover</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hostile takeover">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bash_at_the_Beach_(1996)" title="Bash at the Beach (1996)">Bash at the Beach</a></div>
<p>The match Bischoff promised, a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_tag_team_match_types#Multiple_man_teamed_matches" title="Professional wrestling tag team match types">six-man tag team match</a> billed as the "Hostile Takeover match", was scheduled as the <a href="/wiki/Card_(sports)#Main_event" title="Card (sports)">main event</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bash_at_the_Beach_(1996)" title="Bash at the Beach (1996)">Bash at the Beach</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Center" title="Ocean Center">Ocean Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach,_Florida" title="Daytona Beach, Florida">Daytona Beach, Florida</a> on July 7, 1996. Hall and Nash came to the ring by themselves, leaving speculation open as to who the third man was. Team WCW then entered with all three members wearing face paint as a sign of solidarity.</p>
<p>Luger was injured (<a href="/wiki/Kayfabe" title="Kayfabe">kayfabe</a>) shortly after the match began and had to be removed on a stretcher. The match reached its climax at approximately the sixteen-minute mark, shortly after a late <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#Tag_rules" title="Professional wrestling">tag</a> from Sting to Savage. Savage went on the attack, nailing both Outsiders with repeated axe-handle smashes from the top rope. However, while <a href="/wiki/Referee_(professional_wrestling)" title="Referee (professional wrestling)">referee</a> <a href="/wiki/Randy_Anderson" title="Randy Anderson">Randy Anderson</a> checked on a downed Hall, Hall grabbed his shirt while Nash nailed Savage with a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_attacks#Low_blow" title="Professional wrestling attacks">low blow</a> which knocked both men to the mat. With all four men down, Anderson had no choice but to begin <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#Countout" title="Professional wrestling">counting them out</a> as he did not see the low blow. As he began his count, the fans' attention turned to the entrance area as <a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan" title="Hulk Hogan">Hulk Hogan</a> entered and began walking to the ring to a loud roar from the crowd. Hall spotted him and immediately fled the ring. Hogan, who had not been seen on WCW television for some time, climbed into the ring to chase away Nash and tore off his T-shirt, as he had done many times before.</p>
<p>With the fans still cheering wildly, Hogan stood in the corner nearest Savage and then hit him with his <a href="/wiki/Leg_drop" title="Leg drop">Atomic Leg Drop</a>, stunning the crowd into silence and turning heel for the first time since his <a href="/wiki/American_Wrestling_Association" title="American Wrestling Association">AWA</a> days in 1981. The Outsiders came back into the ring to celebrate with their now-revealed partner as Hogan dropped the leg on the fallen Savage a second time, and after the three men all shook hands Hogan threw the referee from the ring and hit Savage one last time. The official match result was a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#No_contest" title="Professional wrestling">no contest</a> and Savage had to be carried from the ring by an exhausted Sting.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NWoformationBATB96.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="349" data-file-width="465" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/NWoformationBATB96.jpg/220px-NWoformationBATB96.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/NWoformationBATB96.jpg/330px-NWoformationBATB96.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/NWoformationBATB96.jpg/440px-NWoformationBATB96.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NWoformationBATB96.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The formation of the New World Order at <a href="/wiki/Bash_at_the_Beach_(1996)" title="Bash at the Beach (1996)">Bash at the Beach</a> in July 1996</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the match, <a href="/wiki/Gene_Okerlund" title="Gene Okerlund">"Mean" Gene Okerlund</a> came to the ring and interviewed Hogan. During the interview, Hogan exclaimed, "Well, the first thing you gotta realize, brother, is this right here is the future of wrestling! You can call this the new world order of wrestling, brother!". Hogan's statement gave the group its name – the New World Order.</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><b>Gene Okerlund</b>: Hulk Hogan, excuse me! Excuse me. What in the world are you thinking?<br/>
<b>Hulk Hogan</b>: Mean Gene, the first thing you need to do is to tell these people to shut up if you wanna hear what I gotta say!<br/>
<b>Okerlund</b>: I have been with you for so many years, for you to join up with the likes of these two men absolutely makes me sick to my stomach! And I think that these people here (points to the crowd) and a lot of other people around the world have had just about enough of this man (pointing at Nash), this man (pointing at Hall), and you want to put yourself in this group? You've gotta be kidding me.<br/>
<b>Hogan</b>: Well, the first thing you gotta realize, brother, is this right here is the future of wrestling! You can call this the New World Order of wrestling, brother!</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Hogan continued, reminding everybody of the "big organisation up north" where Hall and Nash had come from and that he too had been there and how he had made that company a household name. Hogan followed by bringing up his signing with WCW in 1994.</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><b>Hogan</b>: And then Billionaire Ted, amigo, he wanted to talk turkey with Hulk Hogan. Well, Billionaire Ted promised me movies, brother. Billionaire Ted promised me millions of dollars. And Billionaire Ted promised me world-caliber matches. And as far as Billionaire Ted goes, Eric Bischoff, and the whole WCW goes, I'm bored, brother!</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>He then declared that Hall and Nash were the kind of people he really wanted as his friends and that together, the three of them were going to take over WCW and destroy everything in their path. At this point, Okerlund directed Hogan to look at the debris strewn around the ring and told him that he could expect more of this if he chose to associate with Hall and Nash (subtly suggesting that Hogan should reconsider one more time). Hogan disregarded Okerlund and went into a tirade against the fans while taking another shot at Bischoff and some of the newer talent the fans were cheering.</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><b>Okerlund</b> (pointing at the debris on the <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_ring" title="Wrestling ring">mat</a>): Look at all of this crap in this ring! This is what's in the future for you, if you wanna hang around the likes of this man Hall and this man Nash.<br/>
<b>Hogan</b>: As far as I'm concerned, all this crap in the ring represents these fans out here! For two years, brother! For two years, I held my head high! I did everything for the charities! I did everything for the kids! And the reception I got when I came out here, you fans can stick it, brother! Because, if it wasn't for Hulk Hogan, you people wouldn't be here! If it wasn't for Hulk Hogan, Eric Bischoff, would be still selling meat from a truck in Minneapolis! And, if it wasn't for Hulk Hogan, all these johnny-come-latelies that you see out here, wrestling wouldn't be here! I was selling out the world, brother, while they were bumming gas to put in their car to get to high school! So the way it is now, brother, with Hulk Hogan, and the new world organization of wrestling, brother, me and the new blood by my side... whatcha gonna do, brother, when the new world organization<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> runs wild on you?</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Hogan, Hall, and Nash attempted to attack Okerlund moments later; he threatened to sue if they did. The show closed with the three wrestlers continuing to taunt the fans, who booed and pelted them with garbage. Wrapping up the event on pay-per-view, a still-stunned Tony Schiavone said: "Hulk Hogan, you can go to hell... Straight to hell".</p>
<p>The night after Bash at the Beach, Hall and Nash appeared on Nitro without Hogan, attempting to attack Sting, <a href="/wiki/Arn_Anderson" title="Arn Anderson">Arn Anderson</a> and Randy Savage, but were held back by WCW security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw96_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-wcw96-5">[5]</a></sup> Hogan returned the next week on <i>Nitro</i> and assisted Hall and Nash in beating up Lex Luger and <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_Man_(wrestler)" title="Big Boss Man (wrestler)">Big Bubba Rogers</a> during <i>Nitro'</i>s main event. He then made a challenge to then reigning WCW World Heavyweight Champion, <a href="/wiki/Big_Show" title="Big Show">The Giant</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Road_Wild#1996" title="Road Wild">Hog Wild</a> in August.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hogan_becomes_champion_and_Bischoff.27s_secret_is_revealed">Hogan becomes champion and Bischoff's secret is revealed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hogan becomes champion and Bischoff's secret is revealed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Starrcade-1996-Hogan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="310" data-file-width="240" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c0/Starrcade-1996-Hogan.jpg/180px-Starrcade-1996-Hogan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c0/Starrcade-1996-Hogan.jpg 1.5x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Starrcade-1996-Hogan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hogan won the <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="WCW World Heavyweight Championship">WCW World Heavyweight Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Road_Wild#1996" title="Road Wild">Hog Wild</a> in August 1996, and rechristened the title belt as the nWo World Heavyweight Championship by painting "nWo" across the faceplate</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_(13910528192).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4476" data-file-width="2518" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_%2813910528192%29.jpg/150px-2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_%2813910528192%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_%2813910528192%29.jpg/225px-2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_%2813910528192%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_%2813910528192%29.jpg/300px-2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_%2813910528192%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014-04-04_18-47-00_NEX-6_7299_DxO_(13910528192).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sean_Waltman" title="Sean Waltman">Syxx</a> was the sixth person to join the nWo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At Hog Wild, the newly rechristened "Hollywood" Hulk Hogan (often shortened to Hollywood Hogan) won the match after knocking The Giant out with his title belt. After the match, Hogan rechristened the <a href="/wiki/Big_Gold_Belt" title="Big Gold Belt">Big Gold Belt</a> as the nWo World Heavyweight Championship by painting the group acronym in capital letters across the faceplate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_original_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_original-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwopage_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-nwopage-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoganwcw2_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-hoganwcw2-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within two days of Hog Wild, <a href="/wiki/Ted_DiBiase" title="Ted DiBiase">Ted DiBiase</a> made his WCW debut, declared himself the financier of the nWo, and was given the nickname "Trillionaire Ted".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> On the September 2 episode of <i>Nitro</i>, the nWo got its first defection from WCW as The Giant, who just weeks earlier lost his title to Hogan, turned on his <a href="/wiki/The_Dungeon_of_Doom" title="The Dungeon of Doom">Dungeon of Doom</a> teammates and attacked <a href="/wiki/The_Four_Horsemen_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Four Horsemen (professional wrestling)">The Four Horsemen</a> and Randy Savage.</p>
<p>As WCW's annual pay-per-view <a href="/wiki/Fall_Brawl#1996" title="Fall Brawl">Fall Brawl</a> was drawing closer, WCW was preparing for another battle against the nWo. On the September 9 episode of Nitro, the nWo tricked fans and wrestlers into thinking that <a href="/wiki/Sting_(wrestler)" title="Sting (wrestler)">Sting</a> had joined the nWo by putting wrestler <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Farmer_(wrestler)" title="Jeff Farmer (wrestler)">Jeff Farmer</a> into the group as a Sting clone, complete with Sting attire and face paint. This point was furthered when Farmer, as the fake Sting, attacked Luger, who had been lured into an attack by referee <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nick_Hamilton" title="Nick Hamilton">Nick Patrick</a>. This led Luger, his longtime ally and <a href="/wiki/Tag_team" title="Tag team">tag team</a> partner, to publicly question Sting. At Fall Brawl, as Team WCW was being interviewed, Sting told his teammates that he had nothing to do with the attack, but Luger did not believe him. Going into the match, only three wrestlers on each side had been officially named: Hogan and The Outsiders for the nWo, with Luger, Arn Anderson, and <a href="/wiki/Ric_Flair" title="Ric Flair">Ric Flair</a> for Team WCW. Sting had originally been named the fourth man for WCW, but his participation was in doubt. The fourth man for the nWo was indeed the fake Sting, who convinced everyone (including the broadcast team) that the real Sting was nWo. The real Sting showed up moments later as the last man for Team WCW and took apart the nWo by himself. After assaulting Hogan, Hall, Nash and the fake Sting, Sting left the ring and Team WCW, yelling at an apologetic looking Luger "Now do you believe me?" as he did so. Team WCW, now fighting a 4-on-3 <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Handicap_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">handicap match</a>, lost when the nWo Sting locked Luger in the <i><a href="/wiki/Sharpshooter_(professional_wrestling)" title="Sharpshooter (professional wrestling)">Scorpion Death Lock</a></i>.</p>
<p>The next night on <i>Nitro</i>, an angry Sting laid into his fellow wrestlers as well as the fans for doubting his true colors. He came out unexpectedly, with no music or pyrotechnics, and kept his back to the camera purposely as he spoke:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><b>Sting</b>: I want a chance to explain something that happened last Monday night at <i>Nitro</i>. Last Monday night, I was on an airplane flying from L.A. to Atlanta. When I got to Atlanta, I tuned in the TV to <i>Nitro</i>. And I thought, I was watching a rerun! It was a very convincing film. Often imitated, but never duplicated though! And what else did I see? I saw people, I saw wrestlers, I saw commentators, and I saw best friends DOUBT... the Stinger. That's right, doubted the Stinger! So I heard Lex Luger say, 'I know where he lives, I know where he works out, I'm gonna go get him.' So I said to myself, I'll just go into seclusion. I'll wait and see what happens on <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Saturday_Night" title="WCW Saturday Night">Saturday Night</a></i>, and I tuned in <i>Saturday Night</i>, and what'd I see? More of the same... more DOUBT. Which brings me to Fall Brawl. I knew I had to get to Fall Brawl, and get face to face with the Total Package to let him know that it wasn't me. And what I got out of that was, 'No Sting... I DON'T BELIEVE YOU STING!' Well, all I gotta say is I have been mediator, I have been babysitter for Lex Luger, and I've given him the benefit of the doubt about a thousand times in the last twelve months. And I've carried the WCW banner, and I have given my blood, my sweat, and my <i>tears</i> for WCW! So for all of those fans out there, and all those wrestlers, and people that never doubted the Stinger, I'll stand by you, if you stand by me! But for all of the people, all of the commentators, all of the wrestlers, and all of the best friends who did doubt me, you can stick it! From now on, I consider myself a free agent, but that doesn't mean that you won't see the Stinger; from time to time, I'm gonna pop-in when you least expect it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_original_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_original-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwopage_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-nwopage-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>With that, Sting began a retreat from the ring that would last for nearly fifteen months, and in the process, left his loyalties on the table for either side to try and move him to theirs. The nWo stepped up its efforts to try and recruit Sting, yet never removed the fake Sting from the group. As Sting's character and look evolved, so too did Farmer's nWo Sting character. On the same night Sting made his speech, the nWo inducted its sixth official member into the group, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Waltman" title="Sean Waltman">Sean Waltman</a>, who was friends with Hall and Nash in real-life and wrestled as "The 1-2-3 Kid" in the WWF, now known as Syxx.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwopage_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-nwopage-6">[6]</a></sup> In October, the nWo debuted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_Jones_(wrestler)" title="Mike Jones (wrestler)">Vincent</a>, who had previously been DiBiase's manservant in the WWF as "Virgil", as its "head of security".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_original_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_original-1">[1]</a></sup> Referee <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nick_Hamilton" title="Nick Hamilton">Nick Patrick</a> became the group's official referee after he began showing partiality to nWo members during their matches. <a href="/wiki/Miss_Elizabeth" title="Miss Elizabeth">Miss Elizabeth</a> turned against <a href="/wiki/The_Four_Horsemen_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Four Horsemen (professional wrestling)">The Four Horsemen</a> and joined the group as Hogan's valet. In the storyline, WCW only recognized Hogan, Nash, and Hall as WCW employees due to their holding WCW <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_championship" title="Professional wrestling championship">championships</a>, and the other nWo members went unrecognized as WCW employees; because of this, they were unable to wrestle other WCW wrestlers. This led to the nWo starting a segment on <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Saturday_Night" title="WCW Saturday Night">Saturday Night</a></i>, called <i>nWo Saturday Night</i>, where nWo stable members wrestled local <a href="/wiki/Job_(professional_wrestling)" title="Job (professional wrestling)">jobbers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw96_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-wcw96-5">[5]</a></sup> The nWo also used their "financing" to purchase ad time during WCW programming, which amounted to <a href="/wiki/Do_it_yourself" title="Do it yourself">low budget</a> anti-WCW propaganda, or "hijack" the broadcast signal.</p>
<p>The nWo continued to dominate WCW, with Hogan successfully retaining the nWo World Heavyweight Championship against <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">"Macho Man" Randy Savage</a> and Hall and Nash winning the <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WCW World Tag Team Championship">WCW World Tag Team Championship</a> from <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Heat" title="Harlem Heat">Harlem Heat</a> (<a href="/wiki/Booker_T_(wrestler)" title="Booker T (wrestler)">Booker T</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Ray" title="Stevie Ray">Stevie Ray</a>) at <a href="/wiki/Halloween_Havoc#1996" title="Halloween Havoc">Halloween Havoc</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcwtag_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-wcwtag-16">[16]</a></sup> In the meantime, The Giant stole Flair's <a href="/wiki/WWE_United_States_Championship" title="WWE United States Championship">United States Heavyweight Championship</a> and claimed it for himself. At <a href="/wiki/Halloween_Havoc#1996" title="Halloween Havoc">Halloween Havoc</a>, Hogan's old rival <a href="/wiki/Roddy_Piper" title="Roddy Piper">Roddy Piper</a>, whom WCW had just signed to a contract, came to the ring to confront Hogan. Piper began seeking a match with Hogan the next night.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eric_Bischoff.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="235" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Eric_Bischoff.jpg/170px-Eric_Bischoff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Eric_Bischoff.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eric_Bischoff.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The then WCW vice president, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bischoff" title="Eric Bischoff">Eric Bischoff</a>, who in November 1996 revealed that he had secretly been a member of the nWo all along.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On November 18, 1996, <i>Nitro</i> was live at the <a href="/wiki/Florence_Civic_Center" title="Florence Civic Center">Florence Civic Center</a> in Florence, South Carolina and opened with Hall and Nash physically attacking <a href="/wiki/Brian_Knobbs" title="Brian Knobbs">Brian Knobbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Sags" title="Jerry Sags">Jerry Sags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Rage" title="Robbie Rage">Robbie Rage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Kaos" title="Kenny Kaos">Kenny Kaos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halloween_(wrestler)" title="Halloween (wrestler)">Ciclope</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dami%C3%A1n_666" title="Damián 666">Galaxy</a> and forcing Tony Schiavone to walk off the show after they threatened him. As the show moved into its second hour, Hogan and his entourage accosted Bischoff at the announce table and forced him to say that Hogan was better than Piper, who was still seeking a match with Hogan, but whom Bischoff had not agreed on a contract with yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of the show, Piper and Bischoff began arguing in the ring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-17">[17]</a></sup> As Piper continued to badger Bischoff, The Giant entered the scene and grabbed Piper from behind. He was followed by Syxx, Vincent, and The Outsiders, who all stepped in to stop Piper from attacking Bischoff. Finally, Hogan and DiBiase came out and revealed to the entire world that Bischoff, despite appearances, had secretly been a member of the nWo all along.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-17">[17]</a></sup> Piper and Hogan were booked for a non-title match at <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1996)" title="Starrcade (1996)">Starrcade</a> in December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next night on <i>Nitro</i>, Bischoff permanently left the broadcast booth, and his character became an egomaniacal tyrant as WCW executive vice president, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Manager_(professional_wrestling)" title="Manager (professional wrestling)">manager</a>-type figure within the nWo. At the top of the program, Bischoff issued an ultimatum to the WCW locker room: all wrestlers were given thirty days to join the group. <a href="/wiki/Buff_Bagwell" title="Buff Bagwell">Marcus Bagwell</a> (redubbed "Buff Bagwell"), <a href="/wiki/Mike_Rotunda" title="Mike Rotunda">Mr. Wallstreet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_Man_(wrestler)" title="Big Boss Man (wrestler)">Big Bubba Rogers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Norton" title="Scott Norton">Scott Norton</a> became members in the following weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_original_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_original-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwopage_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-nwopage-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wetpaint_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-wetpaint-19">[19]</a></sup> Japanese wrestler <a href="/wiki/Masahiro_Chono" title="Masahiro Chono">Masahiro Chono</a> also joined the group on December 16 and established himself as the leader of nWo Japan, a sister stable in NJPW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_japan_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_japan-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Starrcade, Piper defeated Hogan. At the same event, after multiple attempts to convince <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Dallas_Page" title="Diamond Dallas Page">Diamond Dallas Page</a> to join, Hall and Nash attacked Page in his United States Heavyweight Championship tournament final match against <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Guerrero" title="Eddie Guerrero">Eddie Guerrero</a>, costing him the match. The nWo left with physical possession of the title belt. It was then given to Syxx, and Guerrero began feuding with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cotc_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-cotc-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-souledout97_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-souledout97-22">[22]</a></sup> The next night on <i>Nitro</i>, The Giant was kicked out of the nWo when he refused to perform a <a href="/wiki/Chokeslam" title="Chokeslam">chokeslam</a> on Piper in an nWo assault.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1997:_expansion.2C_success_and_feud_with_Sting">1997: expansion, success and feud with Sting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1997: expansion, success and feud with Sting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On the January 13 edition of Nitro, DDP seemingly accepted nWo membership, putting on a T-shirt but suddenly gave Scott Hall a Diamond Cutter. At <a href="/wiki/Souled_Out#1997" title="Souled Out">nWo Souled Out</a>, Hogan and The Giant fought to a no contest in the main event due to the nWo referee, Nick Patrick, being biased toward Hogan. The United States Heavyweight Champion Eddie Guerrero retained his title against Syxx in a <a href="/wiki/Ladder_match" title="Ladder match">ladder match</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-souledout97_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-souledout97-22">[22]</a></sup> while The Outsiders lost the tag team titles to <a href="/wiki/The_Steiner_Brothers" title="The Steiner Brothers">The Steiner Brothers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-souledout97_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-souledout97-22">[22]</a></sup> Bischoff re-awarded them the titles the next night on Nitro after claiming that Randy Anderson, who ran in to officiate after Patrick was knocked down, was not the official referee. Bischoff then fired Anderson for his actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcwtag_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-wcwtag-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw97_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-wcw97-23">[23]</a></sup> On the same Nitro, Randy Savage returned for the first since Halloween Havoc. Claiming to have been "blackballed", he hijacked the ring until Sting showed up and they both left through the crowd.</p>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/SuperBrawl#SuperBrawl_VII" title="SuperBrawl">SuperBrawl VII</a>, Hogan successfully defended his title against Roddy Piper. Savage, after weeks of roving with Sting as a "free agent", helped Hogan win. Savage participated in a post-match beatdown of Piper, cementing his place in the nWo. Earlier that night, The Outsiders lost their titles to Lex Luger and The Giant, while Syxx defeated <a href="/wiki/Dean_Malenko" title="Dean Malenko">Dean Malenko</a> for the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Cruiserweight_Championship_(1991%E2%80%932007)" title="WWE Cruiserweight Championship (1991–2007)">Cruiserweight Championship</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The next night on <i>Nitro</i>, Bischoff again returned the tag team titles to The Outsiders, as Luger had been injured and was not cleared to wrestle in the match. Luger, however, issued a challenge for a "winner-take-all" tag team match at <a href="/wiki/WCW_Uncensored#1997" title="WCW Uncensored">Uncensored</a>. Two weeks later on the March 3 episode of <i>Nitro</i>, <a href="/wiki/Turner_Sports" title="Turner Sports">Turner Sports</a> vice president <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr._Harvey_Schiller" title="Dr. Harvey Schiller">Dr. Harvey Schiller</a> "suspended" Bischoff for abuse of his office. At Uncensored, Team nWo won the tag team titles. In addition to winning, per a pre-match stipulation, the nWo gained the right to challenge for any WCW championship whenever and wherever they pleased. At the event, Sting descended from the rafters and attacked the top members of the nWo: Hall, Savage, Nash and Hogan, indicating his allegiance to WCW.</p>
<p>Tensions began to surface within the nWo by April. At <a href="/wiki/Spring_Stampede#1997" title="Spring Stampede">Spring Stampede</a>, the show ended with Savage and Bischoff at each other's throats after the former's loss to Page, and both where forced to be held back by other group members. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_J._Dillon" title="James J. Dillon">J.J. Dillon</a>, who was appointed as WCW commissioner during Bischoff's suspension, later had Big Bubba Rogers and Mr. Wallstreet removed from the nWo due to a contractual technicality. Additionally, Ted DiBiase quit the group after feeling remorse for some of the WCW wrestlers who were victims of nWo assaults. In the interim, the nWo recruited <a href="/wiki/Keiji_Mutoh" title="Keiji Mutoh">The Great Muta</a> on May 26, and <a href="/wiki/Hiroyoshi_Tenzan" title="Hiroyoshi Tenzan">Hiroyoshi Tenzan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiro_Saito" title="Hiro Saito">Hiro Saito</a> several weeks after Spring Stampede; they made occasional appearances on television due to their <a href="/wiki/Full-time" title="Full-time">full-time employment</a> in NJPW. The nWo also added <a href="/wiki/Konnan" title="Konnan">Konnan</a>, whom they dubbed "K-Dogg", on July 14 after he attacked <a href="/wiki/Rey_Mysterio" title="Rey Mysterio">Rey Mysterio, Jr.</a> while Kevin Nash watched.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Starrcade-1997-Hogan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="220" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/81/Starrcade-1997-Hogan.jpg/180px-Starrcade-1997-Hogan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/81/Starrcade-1997-Hogan.jpg 1.5x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Starrcade-1997-Hogan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hogan before defending the WCW World Heavyweight Championship against <a href="/wiki/Sting_(wrestler)" title="Sting (wrestler)">Sting</a> at <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1997)" title="Starrcade (1997)">Starrcade</a> in December 1997</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Bash_at_the_Beach#1997" title="Bash at the Beach">Bash at the Beach</a> in July, Dennis Rodman made his wrestling debut as he teamed with Hogan to take on Luger and The Giant in a tag team match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wetpaint_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-wetpaint-19">[19]</a></sup> Luger won the match for his team by forcing Hogan to <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#Submission" title="Professional wrestling">submit</a> and earned a title shot at <a href="/wiki/Road_Wild#1997" title="Road Wild">Road Wild</a>, set for August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Luger, however, elected to take his shot on the August 4 episode of <i>Nitro</i>, five days before the pay-per-view, and defeated Hogan to win the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Hogan regained the title at Road Wild after Rodman, dressed up as Sting, hit Luger with a baseball bat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoganwcw3_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-hoganwcw3-28">[28]</a></sup> Following Road Wild, the nWo began a rivalry with The Four Horsemen, marked by a skit where they mocked members of the group. The Horsemen responded by challenging the nWo to a <a href="/wiki/WarGames_match" title="WarGames match">WarGames match</a> at <a href="/wiki/Fall_Brawl#1997" title="Fall Brawl">Fall Brawl</a> in September. The match pitted Ric Flair, <a href="/wiki/Curt_Hennig" title="Curt Hennig">Curt Hennig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_McMichael" title="Steve McMichael">Steve McMichael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Benoit" title="Chris Benoit">Chris Benoit</a> against Nash, Konnan, Syxx, and Bagwell. During the match, Hennig turned on his team to align with the nWo. The nWo was victorious after McMichael surrendered in the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wetpaint_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-wetpaint-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bret_Hart" title="Bret Hart">Bret Hart</a> made his WCW debut on the December 15 episode of <i>Nitro</i> and declared he would not join the nWo, but did say he would be the <a href="/wiki/Referee_(professional_wrestling)#Special_referees" title="Referee (professional wrestling)">special guest referee</a> for a match between Bischoff and <a href="/wiki/Larry_Zbyszko" title="Larry Zbyszko">Larry Zbyszko</a> at <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1997)" title="Starrcade (1997)">Starrcade</a>. If Bischoff won the match, the nWo would be given permanent control over <i>Nitro</i>, but if Zbyszko won, it would remain with WCW. On the <i>Nitro</i> before Starrcade, the nWo completely took over the show by tearing down the set and chasing off the WCW announcing crew. They destroyed anything WCW-related and rebranded it <i>nWo Monday Nitro</i>. This event was done as a test run for a permanent changeover of <i>Nitro</i> to an nWo-centric show, with the soon-debuting <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Thunder" title="WCW Thunder">Thunder</a></i> becoming the WCW-centric show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> However, due to abysmal ratings following the twenty-plus minutes of the conversion of the set on live television, the plan was quietly dropped. Zbyszko later defeated Bischoff at Starrcade. Also at Starrcade, Hogan lost the title to Sting. Hogan originally pinned Sting, but confusion arose when Hart appeared at ringside and accused referee and former nWo member Nick Patrick of making a fast count. In reality, Nick Patrick was supposed to make it a fast count, revealing himself to be a crooked official. By Hart's account in his biography, Patrick simply forgot to speed up the count, which left the fans extremely confused. Hart laid out Patrick and ordered the match to continue with himself as the referee. Hogan then submitted to Sting's <i>Scorpion Death Lock</i>, and the entire WCW came out to celebrate the defeat of Hogan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1998:_dissension.2C_nWo_Hollywood_and_Wolfpac">1998: dissension, nWo Hollywood and Wolfpac</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1998: dissension, nWo Hollywood and Wolfpac">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Shortly after Hogan lost the title at Starrcade, the nWo started showing signs of division within the group. Because of the controversy surrounding Sting's title win, J.J. Dillon <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Vacant" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">vacated</a> the title on January 8, 1998 on the inaugural episode of <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Thunder" title="WCW Thunder">Thunder</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup> In addition to the title being vacated, Scott Hall was still slated to face the <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_championship#World_championships" title="Professional wrestling championship">world champion</a> at <a href="/wiki/SuperBrawl#SuperBrawl_VIII" title="SuperBrawl">SuperBrawl</a> as per the stipulation surrounding his <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_War_3#1997" title="WCW World War 3">World War 3</a> win, and this also would have to be resolved with the vacant championship. New WCW <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_authority_figures#World_Championship_Wrestling_authority_figures" title="Professional wrestling authority figures">commissioner</a> Roddy Piper resolved that at Souled Out on January 24 by declaring that since there was no champion for him to face at SuperBrawl, he would face the winner of a second Hogan vs. Sting match at Uncensored in March. Later that evening, the feud between Hall and Larry Zbyszko came to an end when he defeated Hall by <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#Disqualification" title="Professional wrestling">disqualification</a> when <a href="/wiki/Louie_Spicolli" title="Louie Spicolli">Louie Spicolli</a>, who had just signed with WCW a month earlier, interfered. After the match <a href="/wiki/Dusty_Rhodes_(wrestler)" title="Dusty Rhodes (wrestler)">Dusty Rhodes</a>, who had been in the broadcast booth that night and who Zbyszko had asked to come to the ring with him, joined Hall and Spicolli in attacking Zbyszko and joined the nWo, where he served as a mentor to Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehistoryofwwe.com_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-thehistoryofwwe.com-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The nWo continued to expand their ranks into the new year as former WWF star <a href="/wiki/Brian_Adams_(wrestler)" title="Brian Adams (wrestler)">Brian Adams</a> jumped ship to WCW and joined the nWo. Hogan gained a second bodyguard when <a href="/wiki/Brutus_Beefcake" title="Brutus Beefcake">Ed Leslie</a>, who had previously tried to join the nWo at Road Wild in 1996, debuted as a barely recognizable bearded biker dubbed "The Disciple".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_original_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_original-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/SuperBrawl#SuperBrawl_VIII" title="SuperBrawl">SuperBrawl VIII</a>, the nWo had a mixed array of success. Hall and Nash regained the WCW's <a href="/wiki/World_tag_team_championship" title="World tag team championship">world tag team championship</a> from The Steiner Brothers after <a href="/wiki/Scott_Steiner" title="Scott Steiner">Scott Steiner</a> unexpectedly turned on his brother <a href="/wiki/Rick_Steiner" title="Rick Steiner">Rick</a> and manager Ted DiBiase. Scott handed the championship belts to Hall and Nash after the match and celebrated with The Outsiders and Dusty Rhodes, marking his induction into the nWo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> However, Hogan lost to Sting in a match for the vacated WCW World Heavyweight Championship and was attacked by Savage late in the match. After SuperBrawl, Savage then made his intentions clear and declared that he no longer needed the nWo's help to win matches, that Hogan had dropped the ball, and that he was going after Sting to try to bring the world championship back to the nWo. Hogan and Savage tried to one-up each other on episodes of <i>Nitro</i> and <i>Thunder</i> over the next few weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup> which led to a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Steel_Cages" title="Professional wrestling match types">steel cage match</a> at <a href="/wiki/WCW_Uncensored#1998" title="WCW Uncensored">Uncensored</a> in March which ended in a no contest. Earlier that night, Hall lost his World War 3-earned title match against Sting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rift between the different factions of the nWo grew wider after Syxx, who had been out injured since October, was released from his contract and sent to rehab for his ongoing alcoholism. Shortly thereafter, Hall was removed from television; this led to a confrontation between Kevin Nash, Eric Bischoff, and Hogan on the March 26 episode of <i>Thunder</i>. Sean Waltman (Syxx) returned to the WWF four days later as X-Pac and returned the favor, saying that if Hall and Nash were contractually able to do so, they would jump ship and follow him back to the WWF, which led Bischoff to respond with a simple "bite me" on the April 6 episode of <i>Nitro</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nash_and_Sting_at_Nitro_1998.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="362" data-file-width="393" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Nash_and_Sting_at_Nitro_1998.jpg/220px-Nash_and_Sting_at_Nitro_1998.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Nash_and_Sting_at_Nitro_1998.jpg/330px-Nash_and_Sting_at_Nitro_1998.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a8/Nash_and_Sting_at_Nitro_1998.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nash_and_Sting_at_Nitro_1998.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nash and Sting standing opposite each other in the ring, they would later join forces after the formation of the nWo Wolfpac to fight off the nWo Hollywood led by Hogan</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The differences within the nWo were becoming more apparent as Savage and Nash were suddenly realizing that Hogan was only looking out for himself, and the nWo was secondary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup> Nash sided with Savage after Hogan had interfered in a number of Sting/Nash matches, not wanting to have to face Nash to take back his title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup> Nash supported Savage in his quest to defeat Sting, but also agreed to team with Hogan against the returning Roddy Piper and The Giant in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#.28Object.29_on_a_Pole_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">Baseball Bat on a Pole match</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Spring_Stampede#1998" title="Spring Stampede">Spring Stampede</a>, Hogan and Nash defeated Piper and The Giant, but after the match Hogan assaulted Nash. Nash later helped Savage defeat Sting by hitting a <a href="/wiki/Powerbomb" title="Powerbomb">powerbomb</a> on the champion, earning Savage the win, the title, and the ire of Hogan who came out following the match arguing that Savage had "his title".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-savagewcw3_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-savagewcw3-38">[38]</a></sup> Hogan and The Disciple then attacked Nash and Savage to close out the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoganwcw4_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-hoganwcw4-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next night on <i>Nitro</i>, Hogan issued a challenge to the new champion for his title, and WCW commissioner Roddy Piper made the match a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#No_Holds_Barred_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">no disqualification match</a> and said no <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Run-in" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">run-ins</a> would be permitted. Savage and Nash made their own speech later, where Nash said to Hogan "have a nice life" and implied that the nWo was not going to be together, at least in its current form, when the night was over.</p>
<p>Late in the match, while Hogan and Savage were fighting in a corner, The Disciple entered the ring and gave referee Nick Patrick a <a href="/wiki/Neckbreaker" title="Neckbreaker">neckbreaker</a>. While this was allowed, due to the match being no disqualification, it also meant that no one was able to stop Hogan and Disciple from doing whatever they wanted to Savage. The Disciple hit his finisher, <i><a href="/wiki/Stunner_(professional_wrestling)" title="Stunner (professional wrestling)">The Apocalypse</a></i>, on Savage while the belt was draped over his shoulder. Just after this, a furious Nash charged to the ring to aid the fallen Savage. After Nash entered the ring, Eric Bischoff came running from the back and slid into the ring to intercept him. After tossing Bischoff aside, Nash nailed the <i><a href="/wiki/Powerbomb#Release_powerbomb" title="Powerbomb">Jackknife Powerbomb</a></i> on Hogan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw97_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-wcw97-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehistoryofwwe.com_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-thehistoryofwwe.com-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoganwcw4_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-hoganwcw4-39">[39]</a></sup> As the match was still going on, Nash pulled Savage on top of Hogan and went to revive Patrick as Bret Hart entered the ring. Hart picked up the title belt, struck Nash with it, rolled Hogan back over Savage, and revived the referee so he could the <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#Pinfall" title="Professional wrestling">pinfall</a> for Hogan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehistoryofwwe.com_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-thehistoryofwwe.com-33">[33]</a></sup> Although Hogan was WCW World Heavyweight Champion for a fourth time and appeared to have taken the reins of the nWo again, the members of the group itself were now going to have to choose whose side they would be on: his or Nash's.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:K-dawg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="281" data-file-width="379" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/K-dawg.jpg/220px-K-dawg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/K-dawg.jpg/330px-K-dawg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/61/K-dawg.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:K-dawg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Konnan" title="Konnan">Konnan</a> was a member of the nWo Wolfpac, which was led by Nash</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the May 4 episode of <i>Nitro</i>, Nash, Savage, and Konnan appeared wearing black shirts with a red nWo logo, as opposed to the familiar white logo. They called themselves nWo Wolfpac (a name which Nash had previously been using alongside Hall and Syxx to refer to themselves as a trio), and were joined in the following weeks by Curt Hennig, <a href="/wiki/Miss_Elizabeth" title="Miss Elizabeth">Miss Elizabeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rude" title="Rick Rude">Rick Rude</a> and Dusty Rhodes. The Wolfpac became the first nWo incarnation to wrestle as faces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wolfpac_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wolfpac-40">[40]</a></sup> Hogan's side retained the black and white colors of the original nWo and took on the moniker nWo Hollywood, with Vincent, Bischoff, Scott Steiner, Scott Norton, Brian Adams, and The Disciple on his side. Bret Hart never officially joined either side, but supported nWo Hollywood as a member recruiter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_hollywood_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_hollywood-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>At May's <a href="/wiki/Slamboree#1998" title="Slamboree">Slamboree</a>, Nash and Hall were to defend the WCW World Tag Team Championship against two of WCW's stalwarts, Sting and The Giant. However, The Giant joined nWo Hollywood shortly before Slamboree as retribution for Nash injuring him at Souled Out in January. Despite this, The Giant maintained his alliance with Sting, but strongly suggested that Sting had a decision to make in terms of his allegiance. At Slamboree, Hall made his return to WCW in the colors of the Wolfpac for The Outsiders' title defense. During the match, however, he turned on Nash by hitting him with the title belt, which gave the win to the team of Sting and The Giant. The next night on <i>Nitro</i>, Hall was introduced as the newest member of nWo Hollywood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the May 25 episode of <i>Nitro</i> the Wolfpac added Lex Luger, who urged his friend Sting to join him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wolfpac_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wolfpac-40">[40]</a></sup> However, nWo Hollywood made their own effort to woo Sting. Sting revealed his decision on the following week's <i>Nitro</i>, fooling Hogan into believing that he was going to join his side, then turning on him and tearing off the black and white T-shirt he was wearing to reveal a red and black one underneath.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wolfpac_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wolfpac-40">[40]</a></sup> As part of his joining the Wolfpac, Sting began painting his face red and black instead of the black and white "Crow" style face-paint he had been wearing since 1996. At <a href="/wiki/The_Great_American_Bash#1998" title="The Great American Bash">The Great American Bash</a>, the Wolfpac lost two members as Hennig and Rude turned on Konnan following a loss and joined nWo Hollywood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcwtag_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-wcwtag-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_hollywood_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_hollywood-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gab98_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-gab98-43">[43]</a></sup> It was not a total loss for the red and black, however, as Sting defeated The Giant in a singles match for control of the vacated WCW World Tag Team Championship. The next night on <i>Nitro</i>, Sting chose Nash as his tag team partner and the two began defending the titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gab98_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-gab98-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the meantime, a new contender for Hogan's championship emerged in undefeated rookie and United States Heavyweight Champion <a href="/wiki/Bill_Goldberg" title="Bill Goldberg">Goldberg</a>, who had run off an impressive string of victories. On the July 2, 1998 episode of <i>Thunder</i>, Goldberg was granted a title match against Hogan for the July 6 episode of <i>Nitro.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-6"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup> However, Hogan changed his mind and forced Goldberg to wrestle Scott Hall in order to earn his title match. Goldberg defeated Hall and then topped Hogan in the main event to win his first WCW World Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-7"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>After his loss to Goldberg, Hogan turned his attention to celebrity matches for the next two months, wrestling in two tag team matches at <a href="/wiki/Bash_at_the_Beach#1998" title="Bash at the Beach">Bash at the Beach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Road_Wild#1998" title="Road Wild">Road Wild</a>. Hogan won the first match with <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Rodman" title="Dennis Rodman">Dennis Rodman</a> over Diamond Dallas Page and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Malone" title="Karl Malone">Karl Malone</a>. The second match was a culmination of a storyline involving several <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">Tonight Show</a></i> skits involving <a href="/wiki/Jay_Leno" title="Jay Leno">Jay Leno</a> making fun of Hogan, which resulted in Hogan and Eric Bischoff taking over the show and Diamond Dallas Page coming to save the day. Hogan and Bischoff lost to Page and Leno thanks to interference from <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Eubanks" title="Kevin Eubanks">Kevin Eubanks</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kevin_Nash_Nitro_%2798_-_Wolfpac_Hands.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="197" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Kevin_Nash_Nitro_%2798_-_Wolfpac_Hands.jpg/170px-Kevin_Nash_Nitro_%2798_-_Wolfpac_Hands.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Kevin_Nash_Nitro_%2798_-_Wolfpac_Hands.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kevin_Nash_Nitro_%2798_-_Wolfpac_Hands.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fans make Wolfpac hand gestures towards Kevin Nash</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Meanwhile, the feud between Scott Hall and Kevin Nash continued while Nash continued to defend his half of the tag team championship with Sting. On the July 20 episode of <i>Nitro</i>, Hall and The Giant challenged the champions to a match for the tag team titles. Late in the match Bret Hart, who had been feuding with Sting over the previous few weeks, came out in an attempt to attack Sting. Sting knocked Hart to the floor and climbed the turnbuckle to taunt him, but the momentary lapse in concentration enabled Hall to <a href="/wiki/Pin_(professional_wrestling)" title="Pin (professional wrestling)">pin</a> Sting to win the WCW World Tag Team Championship back to the black and white.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehistoryofwwe.com_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-thehistoryofwwe.com-33">[33]</a></sup> The feud between Hall and Nash culminated in a singles match at <a href="/wiki/Halloween_Havoc#1998" title="Halloween Havoc">Halloween Havoc</a> in October, where Hall earned a countout win after Nash left the ring. Nash later stated that he didn't care about winning the match, he just wanted his friend back. On the same night, Hogan defeated <a href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Warrior" title="The Ultimate Warrior">The Warrior</a> when Hogan's nephew, <a href="/wiki/Horace_Hogan" title="Horace Hogan">Horace</a>, interfered and joined nWo Hollywood. Bret Hart defeated Wolfpac member Sting, putting him out of action for about 6 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_War_3#1998" title="WCW World War 3">World War 3</a>, nWo Hollywood attacked Scott Hall and kicked him out of the group for disrespecting Hogan and Bischoff a few weeks earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw98_32-8"><a href="#cite_note-wcw98-32">[32]</a></sup> Kevin Nash won the <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_War_3#Rules" title="WCW World War 3">60-man battle royal</a> and earned a WCW World Heavyweight Championship shot against the still-undefeated Goldberg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> On the Thanksgiving episode of <i>The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</i>, nWo Hollywood leader Hollywood Hogan announced his retirement from professional wrestling and Scott Steiner went on to assume the leadership role in the nWo Hollywood faction. At <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1998)" title="Starrcade (1998)">Starrcade</a>, Nash handed Goldberg <a href="/wiki/Bill_Goldberg#Undefeated_streak_.281997.E2.80.931998.29" title="Bill Goldberg">his first loss</a> and won the WCW World Heavyweight Championship. Hall interfered in the match and shocked Goldberg with a <a href="/wiki/Taser" title="Taser">taser</a>, incapacitating him long enough for an oblivious Nash to hit the <i>Jackknife Powerbomb</i> and score the win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nashwcw1_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-nashwcw1-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the first <i>Nitro</i> after Starrcade, the main event would be between WCW/nWo president Eric Bischoff and WCW's franchise player Ric Flair. This was after months of feuding and weeks of demanding a match against Bischoff for the presidency of the company. Flair declared he would give up all his possessions if he lost. The match was made by Bischoff who believed that Flair would not be able to compete after he had a kayfabe heart attack during a <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Promo" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">promo</a>. Flair defeated Bischoff in the match to become WCW president for 90 days, and Bischoff was relegated back to his old position as an on-air <a href="/wiki/Sports_commentator#In_professional_wrestling" title="Sports commentator">commentator</a>. The ending of the match symbolized a new beginning for WCW heading into 1999 and appeared to be the possible conclusion to the nWo storyline.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1999:_nWo_Elite_and_B-Team">1999: nWo Elite and B-Team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1999: nWo Elite and B-Team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fingerpoke_of_Doom" title="Fingerpoke of Doom">Fingerpoke of Doom</a></div>
<p>As 1999 began, the divided nWo factions were headed by world champion and <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> leader Nash, who was unhappy with Hall's actions at Starrcade, and Scott Steiner, who had taken over nWo Hollywood following Hogan's retirement in November. On the first <i>Nitro</i> of the new year, which took place at Atlanta's Georgia Dome, Nash and Goldberg were scheduled to face off in a Starrcade rematch as Nash had promised on the December 28 episode of <i>Nitro</i>. However, nWo Hollywood accused the former champion of <a href="/wiki/Stalking" title="Stalking">stalking</a> Miss Elizabeth and Goldberg was arrested and taken from the arena in handcuffs. Later that night, Hogan made his return to WCW for the first time since November 1998 and was challenged by the reigning champion. Hogan accepted Nash's request and took Goldberg's place in the main event. In the match, after the bell rang to begin the bout, Hogan <a href="/wiki/Fingerpoke_of_Doom" title="Fingerpoke of Doom">poked Nash in the chest</a>, after which Nash fell to the mat. Hogan covered Nash for the win and became champion again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcw99_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-wcw99-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoganwcw5_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-hoganwcw5-49">[49]</a></sup> After the win, Hogan celebrated in the ring with Nash, Hall, and Scott Steiner, revealing that it was all a conspiracy and the nWo had reunited under what would be known as the "nWo Elite" label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_reunion_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_reunion-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, while Hogan, Hall, Nash, Steiner, Lex Luger, Konnan, Buff Bagwell, Eric Bischoff and Miss Elizabeth were part of the Wolfpac, the <a href="/wiki/Card_(sports)#Undercard" title="Card (sports)">undercard</a> wrestlers in the nWo (The Giant, Curt Hennig, Horace Hogan, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Ray" title="Stevie Ray">Stevie Ray</a>, Brian Adams and Vincent) were still in the black and white colors of nWo Hollywood and never were officially assimilated back into the group. This short-lived group was sardonically labeled the nWo B-Team by fans and commentators. This "B-Team" was a staple of WCW programming throughout 1999 and Stevie Ray was eventually made their leader. This B version of the nWo officially consisted of Stevie Ray, Vincent, Horace, Scott Norton, and Brian Adams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_b-team_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_b-team-51">[51]</a></sup> Konnan was one of the first people eliminated from the group, after being attacked by Lex Luger. He would then align with <a href="/wiki/Rey_Mysterio" title="Rey Mysterio">Rey Misterio, Jr.</a> and feud with the nWo. Sting and Savage, members of the Wolfpac, were on hiatus during the nWo factions reuniting and did not partake in the now-heel stable upon their return.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_nWo_era">End of the nWo era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: End of the nWo era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The reunited nWo did not last long for either faction. nWo Elite/Wolfpac enjoyed initial success with Hogan as WCW World Heavyweight Champion, Steiner as <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_Television_Championship" title="WCW World Television Championship">World Television Champion</a> and Hall as United States Heavyweight Champion. However, they were wrecked by injuries when Hall's foot was accidentally backed over by a car and he was put on the shelf (and subsequently was stripped of the title), while Luger suffered a torn biceps and as a result he and Elizabeth went on hiatus. Luger appeared sporadically in May and June 1999 on <i>Nitro</i>.</p>
<p>Hogan <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Drop" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">dropped</a> the WCW World Heavyweight Championship in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#First_Blood_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">First Blood</a> <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_wrestling" title="Hardcore wrestling">barbed wire</a> steel cage match at <a href="/wiki/WCW_Uncensored#1999" title="WCW Uncensored">Uncensored</a> to Ric Flair and Steiner lost the World Television Championship to <a href="/wiki/Booker_T_(wrestler)" title="Booker T (wrestler)">Booker T</a> after Buff Bagwell accidentally nailed him with a chair. Shortly after, Steiner beat him down and threw him out of the group.
