Scott later reunited with his brother Rick, who interfered on Scott's behalf during his match with Bagwell at <a href="/wiki/Slamboree#1999" title="Slamboree">Slamboree</a> in May 1999. Scott then inducted Rick into the nWo, with Rick wearing a Wolfpack T-shirt on <i>Thunder</i>, and coming out to the Wolfpack theme for his World Television title matches on <i>Nitro</i>.</p>
<p>A month earlier, Hogan suffered a severe injury during a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Basic_non-elimination_matches" title="Professional wrestling match types">fatal four-way match</a> (with Page, Flair and a returned, white-painted Sting with a returned Randy Savage as the special guest referee) at <a href="/wiki/Spring_Stampede#1999" title="Spring Stampede">Spring Stampede</a> for the WCW World Heavyweight Championship, which Diamond Dallas Page won, and was put out of action for three months. It has been debated whether this injury was <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Legit" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">legitimate</a> or not. Nash then began a rivalry with Page, who he blamed for causing Hogan's injury, and defeated him for the WCW World Heavyweight Championship at <a href="/wiki/Slamboree#1999" title="Slamboree">Slamboree</a>. Scott Steiner was forced to go on hiatus due to a back injury and stripped of the United States Heavyweight Championship. Other minor members included <a href="/wiki/Disco_Inferno_(wrestler)" title="Disco Inferno (wrestler)">Disco Inferno</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Flair" title="David Flair">David Flair</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Torrie_Wilson" title="Torrie Wilson">Samantha</a>. Inferno engaged in a feud with Konnan that ended with a loss to him at Spring Stampede (which was the quiet end of his membership), while Flair and Samantha were quietly removed from television following Hogan's title loss at Uncensored.</p>
<p>However, by that time, the nWo Elite had collapsed and no longer had any importance in WCW. As the year went on, the nWo Black and White members slowly began distancing themselves from each other. Scott Norton left the WCW altogether shortly after the battle royal, preferring to stay in Japan where he had begun to build his career. Brian Adams was kicked out of the group and vanished from WCW programming for some time, eventually forming a tag team with Bryan Clark called <a href="/wiki/KroniK" title="KroniK">KroniK</a>. Vincent left the group and joined <a href="/wiki/The_West_Texas_Rednecks" title="The West Texas Rednecks">The West Texas Rednecks</a> alongside former nWo stablemates Curt Hennig and <a href="/wiki/Barry_Windham" title="Barry Windham">Barry Windham</a>, changing his name to "Curly Bill" and later to "<a href="/wiki/Shane_McMahon" title="Shane McMahon">Shane</a>" (as another slap at <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a>). Stevie Ray left the group to reform <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Heat" title="Harlem Heat">Harlem Heat</a> with Booker T later that year.</p>
<p>Hogan and Nash also entered a feud before the end of the summer. Nash lost the WCW World Heavyweight Championship in a tag team match at <a href="/wiki/Bash_at_the_Beach#1999" title="Bash at the Beach">Bash at the Beach</a> in July pitting him and Sting against <a href="/wiki/Sid_Eudy" title="Sid Eudy">Sid Vicious</a> and Randy Savage as Savage pinned him. The next night, Hogan returned to <i>Nitro</i> and accepted a challenge from Savage for the championship; Nash interfered by hitting a <i>Jacknife Powerbomb</i> on Savage and gave Hogan the victory, but the next week Nash attacked Hogan during a match with Vicious and aligned himself with Vicious and Rick Steiner. Over the next few weeks, Hogan and Nash, along with Vicious and Steiner (on Nash's side) and Sting and a returning Goldberg (on Hogan's side) feuded with each other, culminating in a match at <a href="/wiki/Road_Wild#1999" title="Road Wild">Road Wild</a> where Hogan put his title and career on the line against Nash's career. Hogan returned to his red and yellow attire on <i>Nitro</i> shortly before the event and won the match, thus forcing Nash to retire. Nash did continue to make appearances afterward, usually stirring up trouble backstage with Hall as his cohort.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="nWo_2000">nWo 2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: nWo 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In late December, 1999 Nash, Hall, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Jarrett" title="Jeff Jarrett">Jeff Jarrett</a> and Bret Hart reformed the nWo, this time with the colors black and silver. Jeff Jarrett was often accompanied by the nWo girls including <a href="/wiki/Midajah" title="Midajah">Midajah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tylene_Buck" title="Tylene Buck">Tylene Buck</a>. Hall, Nash and Jarrett interfered on Hart's behalf in his match with Goldberg, causing Hart to win the vacant WCW World Heavyweight Championship. After Goldberg accidentally injured himself breaking the nWo's limousine windshield, Sid Vicious, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Benoit" title="Chris Benoit">Chris Benoit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terry_Funk" title="Terry Funk">Terry Funk</a> were left to feud with the nWo. Scott Steiner returned and rejoined the group after attacking Vicious. He later would be accompanied by Midajah to the ring. <a href="/wiki/The_Harris_Brothers" title="The Harris Brothers">The Harris Brothers</a> acted as the nWo's bodyguards before joining the group themselves. As nWo members, The Harris brothers would become WCW Tag Team Champions twice. Hart was forced to vacate the WCW World Heavyweight Championship and went on hiatus from WCW in mid January due to an injury suffered in a match with Goldberg at WCW Starrcade 1999. At the following pay-per view <a href="/wiki/Souled_Out" title="Souled Out">Souled Out</a>, Nash defeated Funk to become WCW commissioner, but his reign was cut short after he suffered a broken ankle and had to withdraw from WCW for a while. Jarrett won a title shot facing new WCW World Heavyweight Champion Sid Vicious at <a href="/wiki/SuperBrawl#SuperBrawl_2000" title="SuperBrawl">SuperBrawl</a> 2000. However, Jarrett also feuded with fellow nWo member Scott Hall after Hall attempted to defeat Vicious and win the title himself. The match at Superbrawl was changed to a triple threat match between Hall, Jarrett and Vicious. Vicious won the match and Hall left WCW for good. Jarrett faced Vicious for the title again at <a href="/wiki/WCW_Uncensored#2000" title="WCW Uncensored">Uncensored</a> but lost. With the return of Eric Bischoff and <a href="/wiki/Vince_Russo" title="Vince Russo">Vince Russo</a> in April, the nWo completely dismantled and Jarrett, Steiner and the Harris brothers joined <a href="/wiki/The_New_Blood" title="The New Blood">The New Blood</a> while the returning Nash joined <a href="/wiki/The_Millionaire%27s_Club" title="The Millionaire's Club">The Millionaire's Club</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wrestling_Federation.2FEntertainment_.282002.29">World Wrestling Federation/Entertainment (2002)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: World Wrestling Federation/Entertainment (2002)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="785" data-file-width="589" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg/170px-Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg/255px-Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg/340px-Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hollywoodhulkhoganwmx8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hollywood Hulk Hogan making his entrance at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_X8" title="WrestleMania X8">WrestleMania X8</a> in March 2002, his first WrestleMania after nine years</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the WWF <a href="/wiki/The_Invasion_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Invasion (professional wrestling)">bought WCW video library and trademarks in 2001</a>, Vince McMahon brought in Hogan, Hall and Nash, the original nWo, at <a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2002)" title="No Way Out (2002)">No Way Out</a> as hired thugs in an attempt to "kill" the WWF so that McMahon would not have to share power with new WWF kayfabe co-owner Ric Flair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> They began by targeting the company's two biggest stars, <a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Steve_Austin" title="Stone Cold Steve Austin">Stone Cold Steve Austin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Johnson" title="Dwayne Johnson">The Rock</a>. Hogan left the group after he lost his <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_X8" title="WrestleMania X8">WrestleMania X8</a> match with The Rock and was assaulted after that match by Hall and Nash. Hogan's comeback to the WWF after over eight and half years had fans cheering him, even though he was a heel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> As a result, he turned face and began feuding with Hall and Nash, with The Rock and <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Kane</a> at his side on occasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup> Hall and Nash then brought in two former nWo members, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Waltman" title="Sean Waltman">X-Pac</a>, on the March 21, 2002, episode of <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_SmackDown" title="WWE SmackDown">SmackDown!</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa, Ontario</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Big_Show" title="Big Show">Big Show</a>, on the April 22 episode of <i>Raw</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The nWo reunion in the WWF/E did not last long, however. During an attack on <a href="/wiki/John_Layfield" title="John Layfield">Bradshaw</a>, Kevin Nash injured his biceps and was put out of action for several months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup> Hall asked for his release from WWE in May 2002, because he was in the middle of a custody dispute with his ex-wife over their two children. This dispute led to Hall getting drunk on an airline flight back from the U.K. and getting into an altercation. Upon returning to the United States, Hall was fired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup> Flair became a semi-member of the nWo after turning on Stone Cold Steve Austin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> As owner of <i>Raw</i>, Flair set up a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Lumberjack_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">lumberjack match</a> with Austin against the newest member of the nWo, which turned out to be Booker T. Booker had just finished a silly skit with <a href="/wiki/Goldust" title="Goldust">Goldust</a> minutes earlier, where he had been wearing a lumberjack costume and fake beard, all but destroying his "tough" momentum going into the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-9"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nash introduced <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Michaels" title="Shawn Michaels">Shawn Michaels</a> into the nWo on June 3 episode of <i>Raw</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-10"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Michaels then literally "<a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_attacks#Superkick" title="Professional wrestling attacks">kicked</a>" Booker out of the nWo one week later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-11"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Michaels, then in the midst of a four-year retirement from professional wrestling, became the first nWo member who had never wrestled in WCW. Michaels and Nash then would set their sights on recruiting <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Triple H</a> (by using threats and demands) into the nWo, implying that they would re-create on-screen their old backstage group <a href="/wiki/The_Kliq" title="The Kliq">The Kliq</a>. This storyline was never finished.</p>
<p>On July 8, Nash returned to action on <i>Raw</i>, teaming up with Eddie Guerrero, X-Pac, Big Show, and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Benoit" title="Chris Benoit">Chris Benoit</a> to take on Booker T, Goldust, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_LoMonaco" title="Mark LoMonaco">Bubba Ray Dudley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spike_Dudley" title="Spike Dudley">Spike Dudley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Van_Dam" title="Rob Van Dam">Rob Van Dam</a>. Seconds after tagging in for the first time, Nash tore his quadriceps after delivering a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_attacks#Big_boot" title="Professional wrestling attacks">big boot</a> onto Booker T, immediately putting him back on the injured list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-12"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> On the following <i>Raw</i> on July 15, Vince McMahon came out to the ring to the entrance of the nWo and made the announcement that the group was officially disbanded as Eric Bischoff became <i>Raw</i> <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_authority_figures#Raw_authorities" title="Professional wrestling authority figures">general manager</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwo_wwf_3-13"><a href="#cite_note-nwo_wwf-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Afterwards, the nWo storyline was stopped and the remaining members drifted apart. Michaels returned to active competition within weeks, Big Show was eventually traded to <i>SmackDown!</i>, and X-Pac was released from his contract.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling_.282010.29">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling (2010)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Total Nonstop Action Wrestling (2010)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="1152" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg/170px-Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg/255px-Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg/340px-Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hulk_Hogan_July_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A reunion was spurred by Hogan's <a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling" title="Total Nonstop Action Wrestling">TNA</a> arrival in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although never again billed as the nWo, the group would reunite in 2010 when, weeks prior to the debut of Hulk Hogan in <a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling" title="Total Nonstop Action Wrestling">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling</a> (TNA), Kevin Nash had hinted that "the band was getting back together" (a reference to nWo 2000 catchphrase, "The Band is Back Together"). On the January 4, 2010 live <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impact_Wrestling" title="Impact Wrestling">Impact!</a></i> Monday night three-hour special, Sean Waltman (Syxx/X-Pac) and Scott Hall made their returns to TNA and with Nash had sought to rehash, to some extent, their invasive alliance (though not legally permitted to use the nWo moniker due to WWE's ownership), with the debuting Hogan (who used an edit of the nWo 2000 theme as his entrance music, as well as all black attire and 5 o'clock shadow). This was the first time in over eight years the members had been seen together at a wrestling event. Hogan conceded the others were his "brothers 4 life"; however, he would decline the offer, stating that "it's a different time". Eric Bischoff then came down and clarified that in partnering with Hogan to run the talent department, everyone would have to earn their spots in the company. At the end of the show, Nash, Hall and Waltman assaulted <a href="/wiki/Mick_Foley" title="Mick Foley">Mick Foley</a>, who confronted Bischoff in the office while trying to get a meeting with Hogan, and beat him down until Hogan arrived on the scene to end the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following week, The Band attacked <a href="/wiki/Beer_Money,_Inc." title="Beer Money, Inc.">Beer Money, Inc.</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Roode" title="Robert Roode">Robert Roode</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Storm" title="James Storm">James Storm</a>), who had asked Bischoff for a match against Hall and Nash, after their match with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shawn_Hernandez" title="Shawn Hernandez">Hernandez</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matt_Morgan_(wrestler)" title="Matt Morgan (wrestler)">Matt Morgan</a>, which led to Bischoff, clearly on friendly terms with The Band, coming out and announcing a match between Beer Money and Hall and Nash at <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(2010)" title="Genesis (2010)">Genesis</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> where Waltman, once again using the ring name Syxx-Pac, replaced Hall after a game of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock-paper-scissors" title="Rock-paper-scissors">rock-paper-scissors</a> for the spot in the match and teamed up with Nash against Beer Money in a losing effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On the following episode of <i>Impact!</i>, Hogan told Nash, Hall and Syxx-Pac that their attitude towards their pay-per-view return was disrespectful. He added that since Hall and Syxx-Pac did not have TNA contracts, they were ordered to leave the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Despite this, Hall and Syxx-Pac kept on returning to the <a href="/wiki/Impact_Zone" title="Impact Zone">Impact! Zone</a> for random attacks and on the February 4 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, Hall and Syxx-Pac turned on Nash and beat him down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Destination_X_(2010)" title="Destination X (2010)">Destination X</a>, Hall and Syxx-Pac faced Nash and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Young_(wrestler)" title="Eric Young (wrestler)">Eric Young</a> in a tag team match, where their TNA futures were on the line; if The Band managed to win the match, they would get contracts with TNA, but if they lost, they would have to leave the company for good. In the end, Nash turned on Young and gave Hall and Syxx-Pac the victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sting_July_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1728" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Sting_July_2010.jpg/220px-Sting_July_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Sting_July_2010.jpg/330px-Sting_July_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Sting_July_2010.jpg/440px-Sting_July_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sting_July_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sting with red face paint, similar to the paint he used during the Wolfpac</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beginning in late March, the group also began using their old moniker of the Wolfpac, as well as the entrance theme used by the nWo splinter group in WCW. TNA was able to do this since the Wolfpac intellectual property was not acquired by the WWF upon its purchase of WCW in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On the March 29 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, Nash offered Young a spot in the Wolfpac. Young refused the offer and in the main event of the evening, teamed up with Rob Van Dam and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Hardy" title="Jeff Hardy">Jeff Hardy</a> to defeat the Wolfpac in a six-man tag team steel cage match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> During the episode, <a href="/wiki/Bubba_the_Love_Sponge" title="Bubba the Love Sponge">Bubba</a> also debuted as the group's personal interviewer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Lockdown_(2010)" title="Lockdown (2010)">Lockdown</a>, Nash defeated Young in a steel cage match. Later in the night, Nash replaced Syxx-Pac, who <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#No-show" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">no-showed</a> the event, and teamed up with Hall in a St. Louis Street Fight, where they were defeated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dudley_Boyz" title="Dudley Boyz">Team 3D</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It was later reported that Waltman had let TNA know days in advance that he was not cleared to wrestle by the Missouri State Commission and was not going to be able to attend the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On the April 26 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, Waltman was found lying backstage in a pool of his own blood, after apparently having been put through a table off screen by Team 3D.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The following week, Eric Young turned on Team 3D and revealed himself as the surprise third member of the Wolfpac, replacing Syxx-Pac.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> On May 4, at the tapings of the May 13 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, after <a href="/wiki/TNA_World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="TNA World Tag Team Championship">TNA World Tag Team Champion</a> Matt Morgan had been attacked by <a href="/wiki/Samoa_Joe" title="Samoa Joe">Samoa Joe</a>, Nash cashed in his "<a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Feast_or_Fired" title="Professional wrestling match types">Feast or Fired</a>" contract, teaming with Hall, and pinned him to win the TNA World Tag Team Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Impact05132010_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Impact05132010-75">[75]</a></sup> Prior to their match at <a href="/wiki/Sacrifice_(2010)" title="Sacrifice (2010)">Sacrifice</a>, Nash invoked the so-called "<a href="/wiki/The_Fabulous_Freebirds#Freebird_Rule" title="The Fabulous Freebirds">Freebird Rule</a>" which allowed Eric Young to be recognized as a champion and allowed any two of the three members to defend the championships at any time. At the event, Nash and Hall defeated <a href="/wiki/Ink_Inc." title="Ink Inc.">Ink Inc.</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jesse_Neal" title="Jesse Neal">Jesse Neal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Moore" title="Shannon Moore">Shannon Moore</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> At the June 14 tapings of the June 17 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, the Wolfpac was stripped of the TNA World Tag Team Championship due to Hall's legal problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The following day it was reported that both Hall and Waltman had been released from their contracts with TNA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On the June 24 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, Nash and Young decided to part ways, as Nash intended to go after Hogan, whom he blamed for what had happened to Hall and Waltman, and didn't want Young to get into trouble for it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Nash was unable to convince Hogan to re-hire Hall and Waltman and failed to secure a meeting with Eric Bischoff, he set his sights on renewing his feud with Jeff Jarrett, who claimed that Nash had tried to hurt TNA by bringing in Hall and Waltman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> On the August 5 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, Sting, who had feuded with Jarrett prior to his 30-day suspension, returned to TNA and, together with Nash, beat down Jarrett, Bischoff and Hogan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> On the August 26 episode of <i>Impact!</i>, Nash defeated Jarrett in a singles match after an interference from Sting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The following week, Nash helped Sting to defeat Jarrett. After the match, Samoa Joe aligned himself with Jarrett and Hogan and drove Nash and Sting away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/No_Surrender_(2010)" title="No Surrender (2010)">No Surrender</a>, Jarrett and Joe defeated Nash and Sting in a tag team match after Jarrett hit Sting with a baseball bat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> On the September 16 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/TNA_Reaction" title="TNA Reaction">Reaction</a></i>, Nash and Sting were joined by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elijah_Burke" title="Elijah Burke">D'Angelo Dinero</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> who claimed to have gotten inside information from Bischoff's secretary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brooke_Adams_(wrestler)" title="Brooke Adams (wrestler)">Miss Tessmacher</a> that would suggest Nash and Sting were right about Hogan and Bischoff being up to something.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Bound_for_Glory_(2010)" title="Bound for Glory (2010)">Bound for Glory</a>, Nash, Sting and Dinero faced Jeff Jarrett and Samoa Joe in a handicap match after Hogan, who was scheduled to team with Jarrett and Joe, was forced to pull out due to a back surgery. At the end of the match, Jarrett abandoned Joe and left him to be pinned by Nash. It was revealed that Nash and Sting had been right about Hogan and Bischoff all along, as they turned heel with Jarrett, Abyss and Jeff Hardy, and in the process turned Nash, Sting and Dinero back to being faces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> On October 13, 2010, Nash's contract with TNA expired and he announced his retirement from professional wrestling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Retirement_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Retirement-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> His last TNA appearance was a taping broadcast on October 14, 2010, when Nash and Sting both announced they were walking away from TNA rather than being a part of <a href="/wiki/Immortal_(professional_wrestling)" title="Immortal (professional wrestling)">Hogan and Bischoff's regime</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="WWE_return_.282014.E2.80.932015.29">WWE return (2014–2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: WWE return (2014–2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NWo_WM31.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3376" data-file-width="6000" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NWo_WM31.jpg/220px-NWo_WM31.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NWo_WM31.jpg/330px-NWo_WM31.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NWo_WM31.jpg/440px-NWo_WM31.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NWo_WM31.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The nWo making their way to the ring at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_31" title="WrestleMania 31">WrestleMania 31</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the August 11, 2014 episode of <i>Raw</i>, which aired on Hulk Hogan's 61st birthday, featured Scott Hall and Kevin Nash as guests. The two shared a moment with Hogan, revealing an nWo shirt hidden under his "Hulkamania" shirt. They were interrupted by <a href="/wiki/Brock_Lesnar" title="Brock Lesnar">Brock Lesnar</a>, who told Hogan, "Party's over, grandpa". Lesnar backed out of the ring when confronted by <a href="/wiki/John_Cena" title="John Cena">John Cena</a>, his opponent at <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(2014)" title="SummerSlam (2014)">SummerSlam</a>.</p>
<p>On the January 19, 2015 episode of <i>Raw</i>, X-Pac (who had joined as Syxx in WCW), Scott Hall, and Kevin Nash came out for a survey segment. They were interrupted by <a href="/wiki/The_Ascension_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Ascension (professional wrestling)">The Ascension</a>, who were beaten down by the nWo, <a href="/wiki/The_Acolytes_Protection_Agency" title="The Acolytes Protection Agency">The APA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_New_Age_Outlaws" title="The New Age Outlaws">The New Age Outlaws</a>. On March 29 at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_31" title="WrestleMania 31">WrestleMania 31</a>, Hogan, Nash, and Hall returned to assist their long-time rival Sting in his WrestleMania debut match against Triple H. The nWo helped to fight off <a href="/wiki/D-Generation_X" title="D-Generation X">D-Generation X</a> (X-Pac, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Gunn" title="Billy Gunn">Billy Gunn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Road_Dogg" title="Road Dogg">Road Dogg</a>), who had interfered on behalf of Triple H. Shawn Michaels later joined Triple H's side, turning the match in his favor, and Triple H would go on to win the match. Nearly six months later on July 24, 2015, Hogan was released from the WWE,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> effectively ending the group's WWE return.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1997, nWo had their own pay-per-view called <a href="/wiki/Souled_Out" title="Souled Out">Souled Out</a>. It was practice for WCW events to have co-brand naming (example: <a href="/wiki/Starrcade" title="Starrcade">WCW/nWo Starrcade</a>) from January 24, 1998 to March 14, 1999.</p>
<p>The nWo has inspired many parody factions like <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Richards" title="Stevie Richards">Stevie Richards</a>' <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_World_Order" title="The Blue World Order">bWo</a>, Eddie Guerrero's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_World_Order" title="Latino World Order">lWo</a>, and the Demon Making Plant, or dMp, in the Japanese manga <a href="/wiki/Kinnikuman" title="Kinnikuman">Kinnikuman</a>. During his time in <a href="/wiki/Juggalo_Championship_Wrestling" title="Juggalo Championship Wrestling">Juggalo Championship Wrestling</a>, Scott Hall, along with <a href="/wiki/Corporal_Robinson" title="Corporal Robinson">Corporal Robinson</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Insane_Clown_Posse" title="Insane Clown Posse">Insane Clown Posse</a>, formed the <a href="/wiki/Juggalo_World_Order" title="Juggalo World Order">Juggalo World Order</a> at JCW's Evansville Invasion on October 6, 2007. To date, fellow nWo alumni Sean Waltman and Kevin Nash have joined this faction for occasional matches. Current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Japan_Pro_Wrestling" title="New Japan Pro Wrestling">New Japan Pro Wrestling</a> stable <a href="/wiki/Bullet_Club" title="Bullet Club">Bullet Club</a> takes some of its gestures from the nWo, like the Wolfpac hand gesture, and have been considered the stable that most closely resembles the nWo since its inception.</p>
<p>Some of the nWo members including The Giant, Scott Steiner, and Curt Hennig, were featured as downloadable content in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_2K14" title="WWE 2K14">WWE 2K14</a></i>. This <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> was released on November 12, 2013.</p>
<p>On October 30, 2014 the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a> entered the arena using the nWo Theme music against the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers" title="Cleveland Cavaliers">Cleveland Cavaliers</a></p>

<p><sup>1</sup> <small>During their reign, Hall and Nash invoked <a href="/wiki/The_Fabulous_Freebirds#Freebird_Rule" title="The Fabulous Freebirds">"The Band Rules"</a> and named Eric Young as a co-champion.</small></p>
<p><sup>2</sup> <small>As part of the New World Order (nWo) storyline, the title was spray painted each time with the "nWo" initials and renamed as the nWo/WCW World Heavyweight Championship, while referred to by nWo members only as the nWo World Heavyweight Championship.</small></p>
<p><sup>3</sup> <small>During one of their reigns, the nWo invoked "Wolfpac Rules" and named Syxx a co-champion due to a legitimate injury to Nash.</small></p>

<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal"><a href="/wiki/Dave_Meltzer" title="Dave Meltzer">Meltzer, Dave</a> (February 14, 2011). "Feb 14 Observer Newsletter: UFC 126 in-depth, Rock and Jericho talk, Strikeforce tourney preview". <i><a href="/wiki/Dave_Meltzer#Wrestling_Observer_Newsletter" title="Dave Meltzer">Wrestling Observer Newsletter</a></i>. Campbell, CA: 35. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/1083-9593" rel="nofollow">1083-9593</a>. <q>Regarding the Kevin Nash deal, as it turned out Nash had signed a TNA contract recently. Nash was always supposed to return to TNA with Sting after they spent most of 2010 building up the storyline where Sting appeared to be a heel to the public and on television only for the reveal at Bound for Glory that it was really Hulk Hogan and Eric Bischoff conspiring to steal TNA from Dixie Carter but Sting saw it coming, but nobody would listen. If you recall, in storyline, Nash and The Pope were the other two who found out because they were the two guys doing it with Miss Tessmacher and she spilled the beans. As you can see, the long-term on that sure held together, given that Pope was turned heel for no real reason before Sting and Nash ever started their comeback. While Nash had agreed to come back, while he denied it, months back, he just signed fairly recently when they were ready to bring him back when he and Sting were to return on the 1/31 show. I've heard several different versions about why things went down the way they did. Dixie Carter publicly admitted she released him when asked for reasons she said were between the two of them. Nash told friends that he signed the contract (he got a significant pay cut because TNA said they couldn't afford his old deal), even though he wasn't happy with the money.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANew+World+Order+%28professional+wrestling%29&amp;rft.atitle=Feb+14+Observer+Newsletter%3A+UFC+126+in-depth%2C+Rock+and+Jericho+talk%2C+Strikeforce+tourney+preview&amp;rft.aufirst=Dave&amp;rft.aulast=Meltzer&amp;rft.date=2011-02-14&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.issn=1083-9593&amp;rft.jtitle=Wrestling+Observer+Newsletter&amp;rft.pages=35&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-98">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.rollingstone.com/sports/news/hulk-hogan-fired-by-wwe-over-racial-tirade-20150724" rel="nofollow">"Hulk Hogan Fired by WWE Over 'Racial Tirade<span style="padding-right:0.2em;">'</span>"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANew+World+Order+%28professional+wrestling%29&amp;rft.btitle=Hulk+Hogan+Fired+by+WWE+Over+%27Racial+Tirade%27&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.rollingstone.com%2Fsports%2Fnews%2Fhulk-hogan-fired-by-wwe-over-racial-tirade-20150724&amp;rft.pub=Rolling+Stone&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
